<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-step-1---raspberry-pi-setup" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#step-1---raspberry-pi-setup"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Step 1 - Raspberry Pi setup</h3>
<p dir="auto">Before powering up the Raspberry Pi, you'll need to install the Raspian operating system (just like Windows/MacOSX for laptops) on the new SD card. This is done using the same process as the quick method used to flash the premade owl.img file, except you'll be doing it with a completely new and untouched version of Raspbian. To get the Raspberry Pi to the stage at which we can start installing OWL software, follow <a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2019/09/16/install-opencv-4-on-raspberry-pi-4-and-raspbian-buster/" rel="nofollow">these instructions</a> from Adrian Rosebrock at PyImageSearch. They are very well written, detailed and if you're interested in computer vision, the rest of the PyImageSearch blog posts are very useful.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE 1</strong>:
At <strong>PyImageSearch Step 3</strong> make sure to create a virtual environment <code>owl</code> (it <em>must</em> be named <code>owl</code> otherwise the software will not load) instead of <code>cv</code> as written in the guide.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>$ mkvirtualenv owl -p python3
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="$ mkvirtualenv owl -p python3" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE 2</strong>:
At <strong>PyImageSearch Step 4</strong> you do not need to compile OpenCV from scratch, the pip install method (<strong>Step 4a</strong>) will be a LOT faster and perfectly functional for this project. Make sure you're in the owl virtual environment for this step by looking for (owl) at the start of the line, if it's not there type: <code>workon owl</code></p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ pip install opencv-contrib-python==4.5.5.62
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ pip install opencv-contrib-python==4.5.5.62" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>

  </div></div>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-step-2---enable-camera" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#step-2---enable-camera"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Step 2 - enable camera</h3>
<p dir="auto">We now need to enable the connection to the Raspberry Pi camera. This can be enabled in raspi-config:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ sudo raspi-config
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ sudo raspi-config" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">Select <strong>3 Interface Options</strong>, then select <strong>P1 Camera</strong>. Select <strong>Yes</strong> to enable the camera. You can now exit raspi-config and reboot.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-step-3---downloading-the-owl-repository" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#step-3---downloading-the-owl-repository"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Step 3 - downloading the 'owl' repository</h3>
<p dir="auto">Now you should have:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>A virtual environment called 'owl'</li>
<li>A working version of OpenCV installed into that environment</li>
<li>a Terminal window open with the 'owl' environment activated. If it is active (owl) will appear at the start of a new line in the terminal window. If you're unsure, run: <code>workon owl</code></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">The next step is to download the entire OpenWeedLocator repository into your <em>home</em> directory on the Raspberry Pi.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ git clone https://github.com/geezacoleman/OpenWeedLocator
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ mv OpenWeedLocator owl
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~

      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>

<p dir="auto">Double check it is there by typing <code>(owl) (owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ ls</code> and reading through the results, alternatively open up the Home folder using a mouse. If that was sucessful, you can now move on to Step 4.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-step-4---installing-the-owl-python-dependencies" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#step-4---installing-the-owl-python-dependencies"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Step 4 - installing the OWL Python dependencies</h3>
<p dir="auto">Dependencies are Python packages on which the code relies to function correctly. With a range of versions and possible comptibility issues, this is the step where issues might come up. There aren't too many packages, but please make sure each and every module in the requirements.txt file has been installed correctly. These include:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>OpenCV (should already be in 'owl' virtual environment from Step 1)</li>
<li>numpy</li>
<li>imutils</li>
<li>gpiozero</li>
<li>pandas (for data collection only)</li>
<li>glob (for data collection only)</li>
<li>threading, collections, queue, time, os (though these are included as standard Python modules).</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE</strong>: Before continuing make sure you are in the <code>owl</code> virtual environment. Check that <code>(owl)</code> appears at the start of each command line, e.g. <code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $</code>. Run <code>workon owl</code> if you are unsure. If you are not in the <code>owl</code> environment, you will run into errors when starting <code>owl.py</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto">To install all the requirements.txt, simply run:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~/owl
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ pip install -r requirements.txt
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~/owl
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ pip install -r requirements.txt" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>

<p dir="auto">If any errors appear, you'll need to go back and check that the modules above have (1) been installed into the owl virtual environment, (2) that Python was started in the owl environment, and/or (3) they all installed correctly. Once that is complete, exit Python and continue with the installation process.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>&gt;&gt;&gt; exit()

<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-step-5---starting-owl-on-boot" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#step-5---starting-owl-on-boot"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Step 5 - starting OWL on boot</h3>
<p dir="auto">Now that these dependencies have been installed into the owl virtual environment, it's time to make sure it runs on startup! The first step is to make the Python file <code>owl.py</code> executable using the Terminal window.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) (owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ chmod a+x ~/owl/owl.py
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) (owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ chmod a+x ~/owl/owl.py" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">After it's been made executable, the file needs to be launched on startup so each time the Raspberry Pi is powered on, the detection systems starts. The easiest way to do this
by using cron, a scheduler for starting code. So you'll need to add the <code>owl_boot.sh</code> file to the schedule so that it launches on boot. The <code>owl_boot.sh</code> file is fairly straightforward. It's what's known as a <a href="https://ryanstutorials.net/bash-scripting-tutorial/bash-script.php" rel="nofollow">bash script</a> which is just a text file that contains commands we would normally enter on the command line in Terminal.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>#!/bin/bash

source /home/pi/.bashrc
workon owl
lxterminal
cd /home/pi/owl
./owl.py
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="#!/bin/bash

source /home/pi/.bashrc
workon owl
lxterminal
cd /home/pi/owl
./owl.py" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">In the file, the first two commands launch our <code>owl</code> virtual environment, then <code>lxterminal</code> creates a virtual terminal environment so outputs are logged. Finally we change directory <code>cd</code> into the owl folder and run the python program.</p>
<p dir="auto">To add this to the list of cron jobs, you'll need to edit it as a root user:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ sudo crontab -e
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ sudo crontab -e" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">Select <code>1. /bin/nano editor</code>, which should bring up the crontab file. At the base of the file add:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>@reboot /home/pi/owl/owl_boot.sh
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="@reboot /home/pi/owl/owl_boot.sh" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">Once you've added that line, you'll just need to save the file and exit. In the nano editor just press Ctrl + X, then Y and finally press Enter to agree to save and exit.</p>
<p dir="auto">Finally you just need to make <code>owl_boot.sh</code> executable so it can be run on startup:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ chmod a+x ~/owl/owl_boot.sh
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ chmod a+x ~/owl/owl_boot.sh" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">If you get stuck, <a href="https://www.makeuseof.com/how-to-run-a-raspberry-pi-program-script-at-startup/" rel="nofollow">this guide</a> or <a href="https://www.tomshardware.com/how-to/run-script-at-boot-raspberry-pi" rel="nofollow">this guide</a> both have a bit more detail on cron and some other methods too.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-step-6---focusing-the-camera" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#step-6---focusing-the-camera"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Step 6 - focusing the camera</h3>
<p dir="auto">The final step in the process is to make sure the camera is correctly focused for the mounting height. With the latest software, when you run <code>owl.py --focus</code> a sharpness (i.e. least blurry) estimation is provided on the video feed. The algorithm determines how sharp an image is, so the higher the value the better. A single script is provided to make focusing as easy as possible. Simply run:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~/owl
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ bash focus_owl.sh 
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~/owl
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ bash focus_owl.sh " tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">This will automate all the steps below. If this doesn't work, follow the steps below. If you would like to focus the OWL again, you can always run <code>./owl.py --focus</code>.</p>

<h4 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-legacy-focusing-1" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#legacy-focusing-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Legacy focusing</h4>
<p dir="auto">With the older versions of the software, you need to stop all <code>owl.py</code> or <code>greenonbrown.py</code> background processes before you can restart the software with the video feed viewable on the screen. Enter the following into the terminal:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ ps -C owl.py # or ps -C greenonbrown.py if you still have the older version.
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ ps -C owl.py # or ps -C greenonbrown.py if you still have the older version." tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">After pressing ENTER, you should receive the following output:</p>

PID TTY              TIME CMD
515 ?            00:00:00 owl.py
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">

PID TTY              TIME CMD
515 ?            00:00:00 owl.py" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">The PID is the important part, it's the ID number for the <code>owl.py</code> program. In this case it is <code>515</code>, but it is likely to be different on your OWL.</p>
<p dir="auto">IMPORTANT: If the headings <code>PID TTY              TIME CMD</code> appear but a PID/line for owl.py doesn't appear it could mean two things. Firstly make sure you've typed <code>owl.py</code> correctly. If it doesn't have the right program to look for, it won't find it. The other option is that <code>owl.py</code> isn't running, which may also be the case. If you're certain it's not running in the background, skip the stop program step below, and move straight to launching <code>owl.py</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto">If a PID appears, you'll need to stop it operating. To stop the program, enter the following command:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ sudo kill enter_your_PID_number_here
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ sudo kill enter_your_PID_number_here" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">The program should now be stopped</p>
<p dir="auto">Now you'll need to launch <code>owl.py</code> manually with the video feed visible. To do this use the Terminal window and type the following commands:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ ~/owl/./owl.py --show-display
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ ~/owl/./owl.py --show-display" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">This will bring up a video feed you can use to visualise the OWL detector and also use it to focus the camera. Once you're happy with the focus, press Esc to exit.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-step-8---reboot" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#step-8---reboot"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Step 8 - reboot</h3>
<p dir="auto">The moment of truth. Shut the Raspberry Pi down and unplug the power. This is where you'll need to reconnect the camera and all the GPIO pins/power in the OWL unit if they have been disconnected. Once everything is connected again (double check the camera cable is inserted or this won't work), reconnect the power and wait for a beep!</p>
<p dir="auto">If you hear a beep, grab something green and move it under the camera. If the relays start clicking and lights come on, congratulations, you've successfully set the OWL up! If not, check the troubleshooting chart below and see if you can get it fixed.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE</strong> The unit does not perform well under office/artificial lighting. The thresholds have been set for outdoor conditions.</p>
</details>

</font></font><h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-command-line-flags" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#command-line-flags"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Command line flags</h3>
<p dir="auto">Command line flags are let you specify options on the command line within the Terminal window. It means you don't have to open up the code and make changes directly. OWL now supports the use of flags for some parameters. To read a description of all flags available type:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $./owl.py --help
usage: owl.py [-h] [--input] [--show-display] [--focus] [--recording] [--algorithm {exg,nexg,exgr,maxg,exhsv,hsv}] [--framerate [10-120]]
                       [--exposure-mode {off,auto,nightpreview,backlight,spotlight,sports,snow,beach,verylong,fixedfps,antishake,fireworks}]
                       [--awb-mode {off,auto,sunlight,cloudy,shade,tungsten,fluorescent,incandescent,flash,horizon}] [--sensor-mode [0-3]]

optional arguments:
  -h, --help            show this help message and exit
  --input               path to image directory, single image or video file
  --show-display        show display windows
  --focus               focus the camera
  --recording           record video
  --algorithm {exg,nexg,exgr,maxg,exhsv,hsv}
  --framerate [10-120]  set camera framerate between 10 and 120 FPS. Framerate will depend on sensor mode, though setting framerate takes precedence over sensor_mode, For example sensor_mode=0 and framerate=120 will reset the
                        sensor_mode to 3.
  --exp-mode {off,auto,nightpreview,backlight,spotlight,sports,snow,beach,verylong,fixedfps,antishake,fireworks}
                        set exposure mode of camera
  --awb-mode {off,auto,sunlight,cloudy,shade,tungsten,fluorescent,incandescent,flash,horizon}
                        set the auto white balance mode of the camera
  --sensor-mode [0-3]   set the sensor mode for the camera between 0 and 3. Check Raspberry Pi camera documentation for specifics of each mode
  --exp-compensation [-24 to 24]
                        set the exposure compensation (EV) for the camera between -24 and 24. Raspberry Pi cameras seem to overexpose images preferentially.



</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $./owl.py --help
usage: owl.py [-h] [--input] [--show-display] [--focus] [--recording] [--algorithm {exg,nexg,exgr,maxg,exhsv,hsv}] [--framerate [10-120]]
                       [--exposure-mode {off,auto,nightpreview,backlight,spotlight,sports,snow,beach,verylong,fixedfps,antishake,fireworks}]
                       [--awb-mode {off,auto,sunlight,cloudy,shade,tungsten,fluorescent,incandescent,flash,horizon}] [--sensor-mode [0-3]]

optional arguments:
  -h, --help            show this help message and exit
  --input               path to image directory, single image or video file
  --show-display        show display windows
  --focus               focus the camera
  --recording           record video
  --algorithm {exg,nexg,exgr,maxg,exhsv,hsv}
  --framerate [10-120]  set camera framerate between 10 and 120 FPS. Framerate will depend on sensor mode, though setting framerate takes precedence over sensor_mode, For example sensor_mode=0 and framerate=120 will reset the
                        sensor_mode to 3.
  --exp-mode {off,auto,nightpreview,backlight,spotlight,sports,snow,beach,verylong,fixedfps,antishake,fireworks}
                        set exposure mode of camera
  --awb-mode {off,auto,sunlight,cloudy,shade,tungsten,fluorescent,incandescent,flash,horizon}
                        set the auto white balance mode of the camera
  --sensor-mode [0-3]   set the sensor mode for the camera between 0 and 3. Check Raspberry Pi camera documentation for specifics of each mode
  --exp-compensation [-24 to 24]
                        set the exposure compensation (EV) for the camera between -24 and 24. Raspberry Pi cameras seem to overexpose images preferentially.

<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th align="center">Flag</th>
<th align="center">Usage</th>
<th align="center">Description</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td align="center">--input</td>
<td align="center">Specify the path to an image directory, single image or video file.</td>
<td align="center">Use this if you want to run the software on images or videos. Useful when testing new algorithms or setting up the software without a camera connection.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><em>legacy</em> --video-file</td>
<td align="center">NOTE: this has been replaced by <code>--input</code> fag. Specify the path to the video file.</td>
<td align="center">This is used when a video file is run instead of the live feed from a camera. It is mostly used in testing new algorithms. If this is not included, a connected camera will be used instead.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--show-display</td>
<td align="center">If flag is present, this will return True</td>
<td align="center">When this flag is included, video feeds and threshold adjustments will appear. Without the flag, the OWL will run <code>headless</code> with no display. This flag replaces the <code>Headless=True</code> variable in the <code>owl.py</code> file.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--focus</td>
<td align="center">If the flag is present, focusing mode is activated.</td>
<td align="center">WHen the flag is included, a Fast Fourier Transform is used to estimate image blurriness. The mean of this value is displayed on the video feed. High values mean it is in focus, low values mean it is blurry.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--algorithm</td>
<td align="center">gog, exg, nexg, exgr, maxg, exhsv, hsv</td>
<td align="center">Select from the list of algorithms to use. Defaults to <code>exhsv</code>. GoG will enable the Google Coral and import 'pycoral' and related libraries. Only use if you have followed the instructions under the <a href="#green-on-green">Green-on-Green</a> section.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--recording</td>
<td align="center">If flag is present, this will return True</td>
<td align="center">Record video to a file</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--framerate</td>
<td align="center">between 10 and 120 FPS, default=40</td>
<td align="center">sets the framerate for the camera.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--exp-mode</td>
<td align="center">off, auto, nightpreview, backlight, spotlight, sports, snow, beach, verylong, fixedfps, antishake, fireworks</td>
<td align="center">Select from the list of exposure modes available on the <a href="https://picamera.readthedocs.io/en/release-1.13/api_camera.html#picamera.PiCamera.exposure_mode" rel="nofollow">Picamera</a>. Defaults to 'sports' for faster shutter speed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--awb-mode</td>
<td align="center">off, auto, sunlight, cloudy, shade, tungsten, fluorescent, incandescent, flash, horizon</td>
<td align="center">set the automatic white balance mode from <a href="https://picamera.readthedocs.io/en/release-1.13/api_camera.html#picamera.PiCamera.awb_mode" rel="nofollow">Picamera options</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--sensor-mode</td>
<td align="center">0: default - automatic; modes 1, 2 and 3 are defined in the picamera documentation.</td>
<td align="center">the sensor mode is specific to the camera. The Raspberry Pi v2 camera has 7 modes, whereas the HQ camera has only 4. Framerate is prioritised over sensor mode. WARNING: high framerates and larger resolutions may 'brick' the SD card. Always backup your SD card before testing new settings, or update from this repository if settings are lost.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">--exp-compensation</td>
<td align="center">Default: -4, use even values between between -24 and 24.</td>
<td align="center">This sets the target brightness level for the camera. Typically it defaults to being overexposed in bright sun conditions so lower values will improve performance.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-changing-threshold-values-in-owlpy" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#changing-threshold-values-in-owlpy"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Changing threshold values in <code>owl.py</code></h3>
<p dir="auto">Other parameters such as selecting or modifying sensitivity settings can be adjusted in the owl.py file itself.</p>
<p dir="auto">To edit this file, connect a screen, keyboard and mouse and boot up the OWL. Navigate to the <code>owl</code> directory and open up <code>greenonbrown.py</code> in an editor. If it's an executable file, it will ask you if you want to "Execute", "Execute in Terminal" or "Open" (see image below). Make sure to select the <code>Open</code> option.</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th align="center">Navigate to the <code>owl</code> directory</th>
<th align="center">Open the <code>owl.py</code> file</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td align="center"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/221152779-46c78fe2-92e6-4e65-9ebd-234ae02c33f6.png"><img src="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/221152779-46c78fe2-92e6-4e65-9ebd-234ae02c33f6.png" alt="owl_dir" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></td>
<td align="center"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/221153072-922d9ed6-8120-4c2d-9bd2-a999030b4723.png"><img src="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/221153072-922d9ed6-8120-4c2d-9bd2-a999030b4723.png" alt="open_greenonbrown_py" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p dir="auto">Once you have opened the file in an editor (this can be a text editor, Thonny, Geany or other code editors), scroll down to the very bottom and you should come across values you can change, such as in the image or written out below.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/221154007-69007ab9-e1b9-4c2f-84dd-efe6b17ff3ca.png"><img src="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/221154007-69007ab9-e1b9-4c2f-84dd-efe6b17ff3ca.png" alt="image" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Editable values for sensitivity:</p>

<p dir="auto">Here's a summary table of what each parameter does. Run <code>./owl.py --show-display</code> to view the output results. Without this <code>--show-display</code> flag the video will not appear on the screen.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE</strong> In older versions ONLY, ff you change the now defunct parameter of <code>headless</code> to <code>False</code>, you'll be able to see a real time feed of what the algorithm is doing and where the detections are occurring. This will need to be switched back to <code>headless=True</code> if you decide to run it without the screen connected. Note that the owl program will not run on startup if <code>headless=False</code>.</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th align="center"><strong>Parameter</strong></th>
<th align="center"><strong>Options</strong></th>
<th align="center"><strong>Description</strong></th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td align="center"><strong>Owl()</strong></td>
<td align="center"></td>
<td align="center">All options when the sprayer class is instantiated</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>exgMin</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer between 0 and 255</td>
<td align="center">Provides the minimum threshold value for the exg algorithm. Usually leave between 10 (very sensitive) and 25 (not sensitive)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>exgMax</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer between 0 and 255</td>
<td align="center">Provides a maximum threshold for the exg algorithm. Leave above 180.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>hueMin</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer between 0 and 128</td>
<td align="center">Provides a minimum threshold for the hue channel when using hsv or exhsv algorithms. Typically between 28 and 45. Increase to reduce sensitivity.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>hueMax</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer between 0 and 128</td>
<td align="center">Provides a maximum threshold for the hue (colour hue) channel when using hsv or exhsv algorithms. Typically between 80 and 95. Decrease to reduce sensitivity.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>saturationMin</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer between 0 and 255</td>
<td align="center">Provides a minimum threshold for the saturation (colour intensity) channel when using hsv or exhsv algorithms. Typically between 4 and 20. Increase to reduce sensitivity.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>saturationMax</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer between 0 and 255</td>
<td align="center">Provides a maximum threshold for the saturation (colour intensity) channel when using hsv or exhsv algorithms. Typically between 200 and 250. Decrease to reduce sensitivity.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>brightnessMin</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer between 0 and 255</td>
<td align="center">Provides a minimum threshold for the value (brightness) channel when using hsv or exhsv algorithms. Typically between 10 and 60. Increase to reduce sensitivity particularly if false positives in shadows.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>brightnessMax</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer between 0 and 255</td>
<td align="center">Provides a maximum threshold for the value (brightness) channel when using hsv or exhsv algorithms. Typically between 190 and 250. Decrease to reduce sensitivity particularly if false positives in bright sun.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>resolution</code></td>
<td align="center">Tuple of (w, h) resolution</td>
<td align="center">Changes output resolution from camera. Increasing rapidly decreased framerate but improves detection of small weeds.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><strong>hoot()</strong></td>
<td align="center"></td>
<td align="center">All options when the sprayer.start() function is called</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>sprayDur</code></td>
<td align="center">Any float (decimal)</td>
<td align="center">Changes the length of time for which the relay is activated.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>sampleMethod</code></td>
<td align="center">Choose from None, 'bbox', 'square', 'whole'</td>
<td align="center">If sampleMethod=None, sampling is deactivated. Do not leave on for long periods or SD card will fill up and stop working.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>sampleFreq</code></td>
<td align="center">Any positive integer</td>
<td align="center">Changes how often (after how many frames) image sampling will occur. If sampleFreq=60, images will be sampled every 60 frames.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>saveDir</code></td>
<td align="center">Path to save directory</td>
<td align="center">Set where you want the images saved. If you insert a USB and would like to save images to it, put the path for that here.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>algorithm</code></td>
<td align="center">Any of: <code>gog</code>,<code>exg</code>,<code>exgr</code>,<code>exgs</code>,<code>exhu</code>,<code>hsv</code></td>
<td align="center">Changes the selected algorithm. Most sensitive: 'exg', least sensitive/most precise (least false positives): 'exgr', 'exhu', 'hsv'. <code>gog</code> will activate a provided Green-on-Green detection algorithm, a .tflite model in the models folder. Ensure you have connected and installed a Google Coral using the procedure <a href="#green-on-green">here</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>selectorEnabled</code></td>
<td align="center"><code>True</code> or <code>False</code></td>
<td align="center">Enables algorithm selection based on a rotary switch. Only enable if switch is connected.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>cameraName</code></td>
<td align="center">Any string</td>
<td align="center">Changes the save name if recording videos of the camera. Ignore - only used if recording data.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center"><code>minArea</code></td>
<td align="center">Any integer</td>
<td align="center">Changes the minimum size of the detection. Leave low for more sensitivity of small weeds and increase to reduce false positives.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
 </details>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-green-on-green" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#green-on-green"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">ç»¿å¯¹ç»¿</font></font></h2>
<details>
<summary><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">å¦‚ä½•ä½¿ç”¨ OWL æ£€æµ‹ä½œç‰©å†…æ‚è‰</font></font></summary>
<br>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-owl-integration" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#owl-integration"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>OWL Integration</h3>
<p dir="auto">Green-on-Green capability is here!</p>
<p dir="auto">Deep learning object detection algorithms for in-crop or 'Green-on-Green' (GoG) require much more processing power than the green detection algorithms we have used previously. If we ran these GoG algorithms directly on the Raspberry Pi, the frame rate would be prohibitively slow. To overcome this, you can use more powerful computers with GPUs (i.e. any of NVIDIA's Jetson series), alternatively you can connect a third party processor such as Google Coral's TPU through the USB3.0 ports of the Raspberry Pi 4. This means increased performance without needing to purchase another embedded computer.</p>
<p dir="auto">The <a href="https://coral.ai/products/accelerator" rel="nofollow">Google Coral USB accelerator</a> is only $59.99, so it provides performance upgrades without substantial cost increases. With the added hardware, there are some additional software installation details that you should follow. And you will need to connect the Google Coral to the Raspberry Pi USB3.0 port too. At the moment, this won't fit neatly in the case, but we are continuing to work on improving this.</p>
<p dir="auto">For all the details on how to install the Google Coral, please head over to the <code>models</code> directory. We have provided an installation script to make it as straightforward as possible.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-model-training" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#model-training"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Model Training</h3>
<p dir="auto">Effective models need training data, so if you're interested in using the Green-on-Green functionality, you will need to start collecting and annotating images of relevant weeds for training. Alternatively, head over to <a href="https://weed-ai.sydney.edu.au/explore?is_head_filter=%5B%22latest+version%22%5D" rel="nofollow">Weed-AI</a> to see if any image data may be relevant for your purposes.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE</strong> There do appear to be some issues with the exporting functionality of YOLOv5/v8 to .tflite models for use with the Coral. The issue has been raised on the Ultralytics repository and should hopefully be resolved soon. You can follow the updates <a href="https://github.com/ultralytics/ultralytics/issues/1312" data-hovercard-type="issue" data-hovercard-url="/ultralytics/ultralytics/issues/1312/hovercard">here</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://github.com/ultralytics/ultralytics">YOLOv8</a> and <a href="https://github.com/ultralytics/yolov5">YOLOv5</a> currently provide the most user friendly methods of training, optimisation and exporting as <code>.tflite</code> files for use with the Google Coral. There is also a Weed-AI Google Colab Notebook <a href="https://colab.research.google.com/github/Weed-AI/Weed-AI/blob/master/weed_ai_yolov5.ipynb" rel="nofollow">
<img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/f5e0d0538a9c2972b5d413e0ace04cecd8efd828d133133933dfffec282a4e1b/68747470733a2f2f636f6c61622e72657365617263682e676f6f676c652e636f6d2f6173736574732f636f6c61622d62616467652e737667" alt="Open In Colab" data-canonical-src="https://colab.research.google.com/assets/colab-badge.svg" style="max-width: 100%;">
</a>
which can be used to train models from Weed-AI data directly.</p>
</details>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-non-raspberry-pi-installation" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#non-raspberry-pi-installation"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">éæ ‘è“æ´¾å®‰è£…</font></font></h2>

<p dir="auto">For the next part, make sure you are in the virtual environment you will be working from. If you're unsure about virtual environments, read through <a href="https://pyimagesearch.com/2017/09/25/configuring-ubuntu-for-deep-learning-with-python/" rel="nofollow">this PyImageSearch blog</a> on configuring an Ubuntu environment for deep learning - just skip to the virtual environment step. <a href="https://www.freecodecamp.org/news/how-to-setup-virtual-environments-in-python/" rel="nofollow">FreeCodeCamp</a> has a great blog describing them too.</p>
<p dir="auto">Assuming the virtual environment is working and is activated, run through these next couple of steps:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>&gt; pip install -r non_rpi_requirements.txt     # this will install all the necessary packages, without including the Raspberry Pi specific ones.
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="> pip install -r non_rpi_requirements.txt     # this will install all the necessary packages, without including the Raspberry Pi specific ones." tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">

</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">It may take a minute or two for those to complete installing. But once they are done you are free to run the <code>owl.py</code> software.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>&gt; python owl.py --show-display
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="> python owl.py --show-display" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>

<p dir="auto">From there you can change the command line flags (as described above) or play around with the settings to see how it works.</p>
</details>
<h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-image-processing" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#image-processing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">å›¾åƒå¤„ç†</font></font></h1>
<details>
<summary><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">å›¾åƒå¤„ç†ç»†èŠ‚å’Œç°åœºç»“æœ</font></font></summary>
<br><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">
é‚£ä¹ˆOWLå®é™…ä¸Šæ˜¯å¦‚ä½•æ£€æµ‹æ‚è‰å¹¶è§¦å‘ç»§ç”µå™¨æ§åˆ¶æ¿çš„å‘¢ï¼Ÿè¿™ä¸€åˆ‡éƒ½æ˜¯ä»ä½¿ç”¨ OpenCV ä»ç›¸æœºè·å–å½©è‰²å›¾åƒå¹¶å°†å…¶åˆ†æˆå…¶åˆ†é‡é€šé“ï¼šçº¢è‰² (R)ã€ç»¿è‰² (G) å’Œè“è‰² (B) (RGB) æˆ–åŠ è½½å¹¶è½¬æ¢ä¸ºè‰²è°ƒã€é¥±å’Œåº¦å’Œå€¼å¼€å§‹(HSV) è‰²å½©ç©ºé—´ã€‚æ¥ä¸‹æ¥ï¼Œè®¡ç®—æœºè§†è§‰ç®—æ³•ï¼ˆä¾‹å¦‚ Excess Green `ExG = 2 * G - R - B`ï¼‰æˆ– HSV é¢œè‰²ç©ºé—´ä¸Šçš„é˜ˆå€¼ç±»å‹æ–¹æ³•å¯ç”¨äºåŒºåˆ†ç»¿è‰²ä½ç½®ä¸èƒŒæ™¯ã€‚ 
</font></font><p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/152990324-d315672c-fb4b-42d2-b4df-363f702c473d.png"><img src="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/152990324-d315672c-fb4b-42d2-b4df-363f702c473d.png" alt="image" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Once the green locations are identified and a binary (purely black/white) mask generated, a contouring process is run to outline each detection. If the detection pixel area is greater than the minimum area set in <code>minArea=10</code>, the central pixel coordinates of that area are related to an activation zone. That zone is connected to a specific GPIO pin on the Raspberry Pi, itself connected to a specific channel on the relay (one of IN1-4). When the GPIO pin is driven high (activated) the relay switches and connects the solenoid for example to 12V and activates the solenoid. It's all summarised below.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/152990264-ddce7eb4-0e2e-4f98-ac77-bc2e535c5c54.png"><img src="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/152990264-ddce7eb4-0e2e-4f98-ac77-bc2e535c5c54.png" alt="OWL - workflow" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-results" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#results"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Results</h2>
<p dir="auto">The performance of each algorithm on 7 different day/night fields is outlined below. The boxplot shows the range, interquartile range and median performance for each algorithm. Whilst there were no significant differences (P &gt; 0.05) for the recall (how many weeds were detected of all weeds present) and precision (how many detections were actually weeds), trends indicated the ExHSV algorithm was less sensitive (fewer false detections) and more precise, but did miss more smaller/discoloured weeds compared to ExG.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/152990178-a53256c0-cfda-46d3-83c8-3ae018b4a40e.png"><img src="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/152990178-a53256c0-cfda-46d3-83c8-3ae018b4a40e.png" alt="results boxplot" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The image below gives a better indication of the types of weeds that were detected/missed by the ExHSV algorithm. Large, green weeds were consistently found, but small discoloured or grasses with thin leaves that blurred into the background were missed. Faster shutter speed would help improve this performance.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/152989906-bcc47ad5-360a-414c-8e25-d9b99875f361.png"><img src="https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/51358498/152989906-bcc47ad5-360a-414c-8e25-d9b99875f361.png" alt="detection results resized" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
</details>
<h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-3d-printing" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#3d-printing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">3Dæ‰“å°</font></font></h1>
<details>
<summary><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">3Dæ‰“å°è¯´æ˜å’Œæ–‡ä»¶</font></font></summary>

æ•´ä¸ª OWL å•å…ƒæ€»å…±éœ€è¦æ‰“å°ä¸ƒä¸ªé¡¹ç›®ã€‚ä¸‹é¢åˆ—å‡ºäº†æ‰€æœ‰å¸¦æœ‰ STL æ–‡ä»¶é“¾æ¥çš„é¡¹ç›®ã€‚ OWL åŸºç¡€æœ‰ä¸¤ç§é€‰æ‹©ï¼š

<li>Single connector (Bulgin) panel mount
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Pros: of this method are easy/quick attach/detach from whatever you have connected, more water resistant.</li>
<li>Cons: more connections to make, more expensive</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Cable gland
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Pros: fewer connections to make, cheaper, faster to build.</li>
<li>Cons: more difficult to remove, more water resistant.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>

<h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-updating-owl" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#updating-owl"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">æ›´æ–°çŒ«å¤´é¹°</font></font></h1>
<details>
<summary><font style="vertical-align: inherit;"><font style="vertical-align: inherit;">æ›´æ–° OWL è½¯ä»¶</font></font></summary>
<br>
<p dir="auto">We and others will be continually contributing to and improving OWL as we become aware of issues or opportunities to increase detection performance. Once you have a functioning setup the process to update is simple. First, you'll need to connect a screen, keyboard and mouse to the OWL unit and boot it up. Navigate to the existing owl directory in <code>/home/owl/</code> and either delete or rename that folder. Remember if you've made any of your own changes to the parameters/code, write them down. Then open up a Terminal window (Ctrl + T) and follow these steps:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>IMPORTANT</strong>: Before continuing make sure you are in the <code>owl</code> virtual environment. Check that <code>(owl)</code> appears at the start of each command line, e.g. <code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $</code>. Run <code>workon owl</code> if you are unsure. If you are not in the <code>owl</code> environment, you will run into errors when starting <code>owl.py</code>.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto"><pre class="notranslate"><code>(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ mv owl owl-old      # this renames the old 'owl' folder to 'owl-old'
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ git clone https://github.com/geezacoleman/OpenWeedLocator        # download the new software
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ mv OpenWeedLocator owl      # rename the download to 'owl'
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~/owl
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ pip install -r requirements.txt
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ chmod a+x owl.py
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ chmod a+x owl_boot.sh
</code></pre><div class="zeroclipboard-container">
    <clipboard-copy aria-label="Copy" class="ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 tooltipped-no-delay d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center" data-copy-feedback="Copied!" data-tooltip-direction="w" value="(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ mv owl owl-old      # this renames the old 'owl' folder to 'owl-old'
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ git clone https://github.com/geezacoleman/OpenWeedLocator        # download the new software
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ mv OpenWeedLocator owl      # rename the download to 'owl'
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~ $ cd ~/owl
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ pip install -r requirements.txt
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ chmod a+x owl.py
(owl) pi@raspberrypi:~/owl $ chmod a+x owl_boot.sh" tabindex="0" role="button">
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon">
    <path d="M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z"></path><path d="M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z"></path>
</svg>
      <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none">
    <path d="M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z"></path>
</svg>
    </clipboard-copy>
  </div></div>
<p dir="auto">And that's it! You're good to go with the latest software.</p>
<p dir="auto">If you have multiple units running, the most efficient method is to update one and then copy the SD card disk image to every other unit. Follow these instructions here. ADD INSTRUCTIONS</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-version-history" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#version-history"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Version History</h2>
